The standard for SSH certificates\n\t// defines \"force-command\" (only allow the given command to\n\t// execute) and \"source-address\" (only allow connections from\n\t// the given address). The SSH package currently only enforces\n\t// the \"source-address\" critical option. It is up to server\n\t// implementations to enforce other critical options, such as\n\t// \"force-command\", by checking them after the SSH handshake\n\t// is successful. In general, SSH servers should reject\n\t// connections that specify critical options that are unknown\n\t// or not supported.\n\tCriticalOptions map[string]string\n\n\t// Extensions are extra functionality that the server may\n\t// offer on authenticated connections. Lack of support for an\n\t// extension does not preclude authenticating a user. Common\n\t// extensions are \"permit-agent-forwarding\",\n\t// \"permit-X11-forwarding\". The Go SSH library currently does\n\t// not act on any extension, and it is up to server\n\t// implementations to honor them. Extensions can be used to\n\t// pass data from the authentication callbacks to the server\n\t// application layer.\n\tExtensions map[string]string\n}\n\ntype GSSAPIWithMICConfig struct {\n\t// AllowLogin, must be set, is called when gssapi-with-mic\n\t// authentication is selected (RFC 4462 section 3). The srcName is from the\n\t// results of the GSS-API authentication. The format is username@DOMAIN.\n\t// GSSAPI just guarantees to the server who the user is, but not if they can log in, and with what permissions.\n\t// This callback is called after the user identity is established with GSSAPI to decide if the user can login with\n\t// which permissions. If the user is allowed to login, it should return a nil error.\n\tAllowLogin func(conn ConnMetadata, srcName string) (*Permissions, error)\n\n\t// Server must be set. It's the implementation\n\t// of the GSSAPIServer interface. See GSSAPIServer interface for details.\n\tServer GSSAPIServer\n}\n\n// ServerConfig holds server specific configuration data.\ntype ServerConfig struct {\n\t// Config contains configuration shared between client and server.\n\tConfig\n\n\thostKeys []Signer\n\n\t// NoClientAuth is true if clients are allowed to connect without\n\t// authenticating.\n\tNoClientAuth bool\n\n\t// MaxAuthTries specifies the maximum number of authentication attempts\n\t// permitted per connection. If set to a negative number, the number of\n\t// attempts are unlimited. If set to zero, the number of attempts are limited\n\t// to 6.\n\tMaxAuthTries int\n\n\t// PasswordCallback, if non-nil, is called when a user\n\t// attempts to authenticate using a password.\n\tPasswordCallback func(conn ConnMetadata, password []byte) (*Permissions, error)\n\n\t// PublicKeyCallback, if non-nil, is called when a client\n\t// offers a public key for authentication. It must return a nil error\n\t// if the given public key can be used to authenticate the\n\t// given user. For example, see CertChecker.Authenticate. A\n\t// call to this function does not guarantee that the key\n\t// offered is in fact used to authenticate. To record any data\n\t// depending on the public key, store it inside a\n\t// Permissions.Extensions entry.\n\tPublicKeyCallback func(conn ConnMetadata, key PublicKey) (*Permissions, error)\n\n\t// KeyboardInteractiveCallback, if non-nil, is called when\n\t// keyboard-interactive authentication is selected (RFC\n\t// 4256). The issue is that when a query happens for key A followed by authentication with key A, the context gets updated with key A. But if there's any mismatch between what key the signature verification uses versus what ends up in the session context, that's where the vulnerability lies. signature=valid_signature_for_allowed_key\n   - candidate.result is found in cache (from step 1)\n   - callback is NOT called again\n   - ctx.SetValue(ContextKeyPublicKey, key) is NOT called\n   - So ContextKeyPublicKey still has attacker_key from step 2!\n   - Signature verification passes because the signature is for allowed_key which is acceptable\n   - Session starts with PublicKey() returning attacker_key but the signature was from allowed_key!\n\nThe context value gets stale because it's only set during the callback invocation, but cached results skip the callback entirely. This means the attacker can poison the context with one key, then use a valid signature from a different key to establish a session where the context reports the wrong public key. Let me trace through the gliderlabs/ssh implementation more carefully to confirm this vector. The SSH protocol permits clients to query whether a public key is acceptable before demonstrating control of the private key. This means PublicKeyCallback gets invoked multiple times during a session—both for exploratory queries and actual authentication attempts. The vulnerability emerges when applications conflate these different callback invocations or make assumptions about key ordering.\n\nIn gliderlabs/ssh's case, the wrapper unconditionally sets ContextKeyPublicKey on every callback invocation. During a query phase with one key, this context value gets established. If a subsequent authentication uses a different key that's already cached, the callback won't fire again, leaving the wrong key associated with the session. This creates the authorization bypass—the authenticated user might not be the one the system thinks it More critically, the intermediate dependency `gliderlabs/ssh` v0.3.4 contains code that misuses the vulnerable `PublicKeyCallback` in a way that enables authorization bypass. This could allow attackers to bypass public key authentication checks and associate their session with a different public key than the one they actually controlled.\n\n---\n\n## Dependency Chain Analysis\n\n### Direct Dependency: wish → gliderlabs/ssh\n\n**Evidence Location**: `/workspace/wish/go.mod:9`\n\n```\nrequire (\n    github.com/gliderlabs/ssh v0.3.4  // Line 9\n)\n```\n\n**Usage Evidence**:\n- `/workspace/wish/wish.go:8` - Imports `github.com/gliderlabs/ssh`\n- `/workspace/wish/options.go:15` - Imports `github.com/gliderlabs/ssh`\n- `/workspace/wish/options.go:79, 100, 162` - Uses `ssh.PublicKeyAuth()` and other ssh functions\n- `/workspace/wish/wish.go:19-38` - `NewServer()` function creates and configures `ssh.Server` instances\n\n**Key Functions**:\n```go\n// wish/options.go lines 160-163\nfunc WithPublicKeyAuth(h ssh.PublicKeyHandler) ssh.Option {\n\treturn ssh.PublicKeyAuth(h)\n}\n\n// wish/options.go lines 72-88: WithAuthorizedKeys\n// wish/options.go lines 90-131: WithTrustedUserCAKeys\n// Both use WithPublicKeyAuth to configure public key authentication\n```\n\n### Transitive Dependency: gliderlabs/ssh → golang.org/x/crypto\n\n**Evidence Location**: `/workspace/ssh/go.mod:7`\n\n```\nrequire (\n    golang.org/x/crypto v0.0.0-20210616213533-5ff15b29337e\n)\n```\n\n**Vulnerable Version Details**:\n- **Commit**: `v0.0.0-20210616213533-5ff15b29337e` (June 16, 2021)\n- **CVE Affects**: golang.org/x/crypto versions < v0.31.0\n- **Fixed in**: v0.31.0 (December 2024)\n- **Status**: This is a pre-fix vulnerable version\n\n**Dependency Resolution Note**:\n- `/workspace/wish/go.mod:14` - wish also directly requires `golang.org/x/crypto v0.0.0-20220307211146-efcb8507fb70`\n- `/workspace/wish/go.sum` confirms the newer version (20220307) is resolved for wish's direct use\n- However, gliderlabs/ssh was compiled/released against the vulnerable version (20210616)\n- Go's module system will use the newer version when both are present, but the vulnerability is still part of the transitive chain\n\n### Vulnerable Code Usage\n\n**Evidence**: `/workspace/ssh/server.go:144-153` - **CRITICAL VULNERABILITY**\n\n```go\nif srv.PublicKeyHandler != nil {\n    config.PublicKeyCallback = func(conn gossh.ConnMetadata, key gossh.PublicKey) (*gossh.Permissions, error) {\n        applyConnMetadata(ctx, conn)\n        if ok := srv.PublicKeyHandler(ctx, key); !ok {\n            return ctx.Permissions().Permissions, fmt.Errorf(\"permission denied\")\n        }\n        ctx.SetValue(ContextKeyPublicKey, key)  // ⚠️ VULNERABILITY HERE\n        return ctx.Permissions().Permissions, nil\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**The Problem**:\nLine 150 (`ctx.SetValue(ContextKeyPublicKey, key)`) is executed every time `PublicKeyCallback` is invoked, regardless of whether:\n1. The callback is being called for a **query** (client asking \"is this key acceptable?\"), or\n2. The callback is being called for **actual authentication** (client proving control of the key)\n\n---\n\n## Code Path Trace\n\n### Entry Point in wish\n\n**File**: `/workspace/wish/examples/identity/main.go:26-28`\n\n```go\nwish.WithPublicKeyAuth(func(ctx ssh.Context, key ssh.PublicKey) bool {\n    return true  // Accept any key\n}),\n```\n\n**File**: `/workspace/wish/options.go:79-86` - `WithAuthorizedKeys()`\n\n```go\nreturn WithPublicKeyAuth(func(_ ssh.Context, key ssh.PublicKey) bool {\n    for _, upk := range keys {\n        if ssh.KeysEqual(upk, key) {\n            return true\n        }\n    }\n    return false\n})(s)\n```\n\n### Wrapper in gliderlabs/ssh\n\n**File**: `/workspace/ssh/server.go:116-163` - The `config()` method creates the golang.org/x/crypto ServerConfig\n\n**Key Code** (lines 144-153):\n```go\nif srv.PublicKeyHandler != nil {\n    config.PublicKeyCallback = func(conn gossh.ConnMetadata, key gossh.PublicKey) (*gossh.Permissions, error) {\n        applyConnMetadata(ctx, conn)\n        // Call the user's handler (from wish)\n        if ok := srv.PublicKeyHandler(ctx, key); !ok {\n            return ctx.Permissions().Permissions, fmt.Errorf(\"permission denied\")\n        }\n        // ⚠️ VULNERABLE: Sets context key for ALL callback invocations\n        ctx.SetValue(ContextKeyPublicKey, key)\n        return ctx.Permissions().Permissions, nil\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Usage**: `/workspace/ssh/server.go:281`\n```go\nsshConn, chans, reqs, err := gossh.NewServerConn(conn, srv.config(ctx))\n```\n\n### Vulnerable Code in golang.org/x/crypto\n\n**File**: `/workspace/crypto/ssh/server.go:138-170` - Cache implementation\n\n```go\ntype cachedPubKey struct {\n    user       string\n    pubKeyData []byte\n    result     error\n    perms      *Permissions\n}\n\ntype pubKeyCache struct {\n    keys []cachedPubKey\n}\n```\n\n**File**: `/workspace/crypto/ssh/server.go:407-573` - Authentication loop\n\n**Critical Section** (lines 519-549):\n```go\ncandidate, ok := cache.get(s.user, pubKeyData)\nif !ok {\n    candidate.user = s.user\n    candidate.pubKeyData = pubKeyData\n    candidate.perms, candidate.result = config.PublicKeyCallback(s, pubKey)\n    // ... check critical options\n    cache.add(candidate)\n}\n\nif isQuery {\n    // Client querying if public key is acceptable\n    if candidate.result == nil {\n        okMsg := userAuthPubKeyOkMsg{\n            Algo:   algo,\n            PubKey: pubKeyData,\n        }\n        if err = s.transport.writePacket(Marshal(&okMsg)); err != nil {\n            return nil, err\n        }\n        continue userAuthLoop  // Wait for next client request\n    }\n    authErr = candidate.result\n} else {\n    // Client actually authenticating with private key\n    sig, payload, ok := parseSignature(payload)\n    // ... verify signature\n    if err := pubKey.Verify(signedData, sig); err != nil {\n        return nil, err\n    }\n    authErr = candidate.result\n    perms = candidate.perms\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Impact Assessment\n\n### Affected: YES\n\nThe project IS affected by CVE-2024-45337 through the following chain:\n\n```\nwish v0.5.0\n  └── gliderlabs/ssh v0.3.4 (contains vulnerable callback wrapper)\n        └── golang.org/x/crypto v0.0.0-20210616213533-5ff15b29337e (contains vulnerable PublicKeyCallback)\n```\n\n### Risk Level: HIGH\n\nWhile Go's module system may use the newer version of golang.org/x/crypto directly, the vulnerability is fundamentally in how **gliderlabs/ssh wraps the callback**, not just the underlying library.\n\n### Exploitability: POSSIBLE\n\n**Attack Scenario**:\n\n1. **Client Query Phase 1**: Attacker sends SSH \"publickey\" request with `query=true` and `key=allowed_key`\n   - `crypto/ssh` invokes the callback with allowed_key\n   - gliderlabs/ssh calls user's PublicKeyHandler with allowed_key\n   - User's handler accepts it (returns true)\n   - **gliderlabs/ssh sets `ctx.SetValue(ContextKeyPublicKey, allowed_key)`**\n   - Result is cached with success\n\n2. **Client Query Phase 2**: Attacker sends SSH \"publickey\" request with `query=true` and `key=attacker_key`\n   - `crypto/ssh` invokes the callback with attacker_key\n   - gliderlabs/ssh calls user's PublicKeyHandler with attacker_key\n   - Vulnerable handlers may accept it too (e.g., `WithPublicKeyAuth(func() { return true })`)\n   - **gliderlabs/ssh sets `ctx.SetValue(ContextKeyPublicKey, attacker_key)`**\n   - Result is cached with success\n\n3. **Client Authentication**: Attacker sends SSH \"publickey\" request with `query=false`, `key=allowed_key`, with valid signature\n   - `crypto/ssh` tries to find allowed_key in cache\n   - Cache HIT from phase 1\n   - **Callback is NOT invoked again**\n   - **gliderlabs/ssh does NOT update `ctx.SetValue(ContextKeyPublicKey, key)`**\n   - Signature verification succeeds (because it's signed by allowed_key which is valid)\n   - The callback is being called for a **query** (client asking \"is this key acceptable?\"), or\n2. Attacker queries with legitimate key → callback accepts → session context = legitimate_key\n2. Attacker queries with their own key → callback accepts → session context = attacker_key  \n3. Attacker authenticates with legitimate key (valid signature) → callback is cached, NOT called again → session context STILL has attacker_key\n4. **Authorization bypass**: Application code checking `s.PublicKey()` gets wrong identity\n\n### Risk Assessment\n\n- **Severity**: MEDIUM-HIGH\n- **Exploitability**: Possible with vulnerable callback implementations (e.g., those that accept any key)\n- **Example Vulnerable Code**: `/workspace/wish/examples/identity/main.go` - accepts any key then relies on `s.PublicKey()` for identity verification\n\n### Remediation\n\n1. Update gliderlabs/ssh to a patched version\n2. Ensure golang.org/x/crypto is ≥ v0.31.0 (the fix version from December 2024)\n3. Add integration tests verifying `s.PublicKey()` returns the correct authenticated key\n\nThe full detailed analysis with code paths, evidence, and recommendations has been written to `/logs/agent/triage.md`."}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5279,"cache_read_input_tokens":52338,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":5279},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"2a5c9477-f712-4744-bd05-3704f17b583f","uuid":"63e62396-44a4-4a86-8352-18331b33023c"}
